<div id="review_1103162382" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1103162382" />
    <a title="Shelly Strange" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25393430-shelly-strange"><img alt="Shelly Strange" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600285315p2/25393430.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1103162382?book_show_action=true">Nov 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shelly Strange" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shelly Strange" href="/user/show/25393430-shelly-strange">Shelly Strange</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=read-2014">read-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=hot-guys-alphas-rawr">hot-guys-alphas-rawr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=fantasy-paranormal">fantasy-paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=3-stars">3-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=fantasy-vampires">fantasy-vampires</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1103162382" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6697873801817943993"><b>August 17, 2018: On sale for $2.99</b> - Recommended for established fans of the series.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1415996948ra/11874343.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Everyone who has read The Vampire Chronicles knows it’s been over ten years since a book in the series was been released. Anne Rice thought she was done with the series and then came up recently with an idea for another book and here we are: Prince Lestat (#11 in the series).<br/><br/>Most prolific readers are also probably aware of the controversies involving Rice (petitioning to force reviewers to use their real names an</span>
  <span id="freeText6697873801817943993" style="display:none"><b>August 17, 2018: On sale for $2.99</b> - Recommended for established fans of the series.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1415996948ra/11874343.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Everyone who has read The Vampire Chronicles knows it’s been over ten years since a book in the series was been released. Anne Rice thought she was done with the series and then came up recently with an idea for another book and here we are: Prince Lestat (#11 in the series).<br><br>Most prolific readers are also probably aware of the controversies involving Rice (petitioning to force reviewers to use their real names and using the internet and her People of the Page to oppose negative reviewers as being bullies or trolls). I disagree with her stance on those issues, but I decided to give this book a chance, and I’m glad I did.<br><br>Like millions of other people, reading The Vampire Chronicles was a rite of passage for me in my teens, and there’s no doubt in my mind, it largely contributed in a positive way to my love for reading. I haven’t re-read any of the earlier books in over a decade. So this was *almost* like a new experience.<br><br>However, I was easily drawn back in to the familiar characters, and they are all present here. Besides the obvious main character, Lestat, we get to see Louis, Armand, Marius, Pandora, Jesse, David, Maharet, Mekare, Gabrielle, Daniel, and many, many other new and obscure vampires.<br><br>The book seems to mainly focus on the “ancients,” the old vampires. But almost all vampires everywhere are hearing a “Voice,” telepathically urging and ordering them to burn and destroy young vampires all over the world. If the older ones are not using their “Fire Gift” to destroy the young ones, “The Voice” is manipulating the young ones to kill and turn on each other. So the vampire population is being reduced dramatically.<br><br>Part 2, The Open Highway through the Savage Garden, was the slowest and longest section. I understand the need for it because otherwise the vampires in these chapters showing up at Trinity Gate towards the end would make no sense. But it was essentially a bunch of short stories involving mainly obscure vampires from the chronicles who were never given names or only mentioned briefly. The chapters were somewhat interesting, but these were sections where you could see that Rice’s style has not changed, her ancient vampires have not changed much or adapted to modern times (besides maybe learning to operate a flat screen tv or computer). They still listen to classical music and wear clothes out of Renaissance times (ok so maybe some of them wear designer suits); they still talk like people living hundreds of years ago would talk, use flowery sentences, etc. They all seem to like the same types of living quarters and entertainment. <br><br>And I’m not sure why (maybe this was explained in other books) but about 90% of Rice’s vampires only hang out in same-sex groups. There was only one male character who had a “Blood Wife.” It just seems strange to me, as it would be strange if every character only had opposite sex partners. It’s only until we get to around Chapter 18 that we start to see female vampires in any significant portion of the story. This is a mainly male character-driven book.<br><br>Overall, this was enjoyable. Rice took it a bit (arguably) too far in using science to come up with one subplot <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[With a vampire scientist’s help, Lestat has sex, produces viable sperm, and ends up with a son (unbeknownst at first to him)  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. It didn’t bother me, though. I don’t expect realism with my fantasy. But it was definitely “fanciful.”<br><br>If you didn’t like Rice’s work before, you probably still won’t like it. If you had gotten tired of The Vampire Chronicles before, you probably are not going to suddenly start loving them again after reading this. <br><br>One thing I noticed that I hadn’t before…was Armand always such a huge d!@k?! I think he is my least favorite vampire now and I remembered liking his book back when it came out.<br><br>Another thing that bugged me is how it’s such a big deal that the vampires of this series have a “hierarchy” and need to be controlled and have a “leader.” It seems a little contrived. It’s basically reiterated over and over how the elders have to come together and they need a leader (of course it’s going to be Lestat). By the end, Marius is set to draw up a code of laws even! #eyeroll<br><br>I also don’t understand why everyone was so instantly willing to let Lestat be their leader and almost unanimously and unquestioningly supported him? It was a little too convenient. The Brat Prince is suddenly insta-loved by everyone, not just the ones who remembered him as the sexy, popular rock star of the 90s. “He is all that anyone ever said he was.” Lestat found him some fanboys! <br><br>And then when they figure out who The Voice is and what is going to happen, they sit around and *talk* about it for pages and pages and pages. By that point, you already know, so it slowed the pace down too much for my tastes. Well, I guess I actually can believe that the others were so willing to give the reins to Lestat, since they just want to sit around and talk.<br><br>The ending was predictable. I feel the book started off strong, but ended up just being an okay book. I’m glad I read it. It certainly wasn’t an awful book, in my view, and it made me happy to read about these favorite characters again. I guess Lestat seems to have grown up in this one. There are still some stories that could be told after this if Rice chooses, in particular with new characters Rose and Viktor. <br><br>(Longest review ever, sorry.)</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="6697873801817943993" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1091588557" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1091588557" />
    <a title="planetkimi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/680012-planetkimi"><img alt="planetkimi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1199081186p2/680012.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1091588557?book_show_action=true">Oct 28, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="planetkimi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="planetkimi" href="/user/show/680012-planetkimi">planetkimi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/680012-planetkimi?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/680012-planetkimi?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1091588557" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3422883930262670366">Having just finished <i>Prince Lestat</i>, I want now want to go back and reread The <i>Vampire Lestat</i> and <i>The Queen of the Damned</i>. When people ask about “favorite books,” “books that influenced your life,” “top 10 books you’d have on a desert island,” etc, <i>The Vampire Lestat</i> tops my list. But while my memory of it remains strongly positive, it’s been some time since I’ve actually read it. After finishing <i>Prince Lestat</i>, I wonder if my tastes have changed, or if Rice’s writing has changed. Unfortunately Pr</span>
  <span id="freeText3422883930262670366" style="display:none">Having just finished <i>Prince Lestat</i>, I want now want to go back and reread The <i>Vampire Lestat</i> and <i>The Queen of the Damned</i>. When people ask about “favorite books,” “books that influenced your life,” “top 10 books you’d have on a desert island,” etc, <i>The Vampire Lestat</i> tops my list. But while my memory of it remains strongly positive, it’s been some time since I’ve actually read it. After finishing <i>Prince Lestat</i>, I wonder if my tastes have changed, or if Rice’s writing has changed. Unfortunately Prince Lestat didn’t line up with my expectations - or my memory. <br /><br />In the 400+ page book, there’s a lot of talking. And weeping. Vampires apparently cry a lot for reasons that are frequently not fully explained. I feel like the novel is really a series of verbal paintings strung together - Rice wants to carefully construct visually emotional scenes, but doesn’t flesh out the motivations and history that leads the reader to feel the impact of the scene. We’re just told that so-and-so was sad. Or anciently inscrutable. Or just sitting there being beautiful.<br /><br />I didn’t find much to sympathize with in most of the characters. More of a refresher of their distinct personalities and motivations would have been welcome. For example, we’re told that Armand is dangerous and menacing, but not reminded why. Several vampires are resurrected from the pages of prior Vampire Chronicles for the apparent reason of just being present and seen - they don’t materially add to the story. Given the history some characters have together, it seems that the inevitable vampire reunion would have been ripe for thrilling drama. It isn’t. <br /><br />I also think I miss the sense of struggle. One of the aspects of Lestat that I enjoy the most is that he’s an outsider fighting to make sense of things on his own terms. There is a threat in this book, sure, but he figures out what’s going on soon enough without the relentless pursuit and conflict that characterize Lestat’s earlier adventures. It’s also pretty clear that he can no longer be considered an outsider.<br /><br />I think that Rice’s greatest strengths are her myth-making and existential conflicts. Her origin story for vampires is iconic. Her presentation of other supernatural beings (witches, spirits, djinn, mummies) is fantastically original. The novels that explore the morality of preying on humans and the nature of evil are thoughtful and captivating. <i>Prince Lestat</i> does not capitalize on those strengths and I regrettably find it to be a shadow of its predecessors.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3422883930262670366" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2225246-darcy?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2225246-darcy?shelf=uf">uf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2225246-darcy?shelf=listened-to-at-work">listened-to-at-work</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2225246-darcy?shelf=audio-book">audio-book</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer888428522" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5241689122916487353">When I saw that Rice was writing more in this series my first instinct was excitement, I so loved this series. My copies are so worn, spines cracked, to the point pages are close to falling out, pages yellowed and corners dog eared from being read so many times. My second thought on seeing an addition to this series was, it's been a long time, Rice found God and eschewed all of this, plus I had been dnf'ing her latest books, so I was leery, very leery.<br/><br/>After listening to 40% of the book I'm throw</span>
  <span id="freeText5241689122916487353" style="display:none">When I saw that Rice was writing more in this series my first instinct was excitement, I so loved this series. My copies are so worn, spines cracked, to the point pages are close to falling out, pages yellowed and corners dog eared from being read so many times. My second thought on seeing an addition to this series was, it's been a long time, Rice found God and eschewed all of this, plus I had been dnf'ing her latest books, so I was leery, very leery.<br /><br />After listening to 40% of the book I'm throwing in the towel. Parts of the book were interesting, the ones with the characters that we loved from the past books. But the timeline is so very vast, even in only the 40% that I read. What ultimately ended up turning me off was the obscure characters that get a lot of page time. Heck I don't remember them at all, then Rice will mention their connection and it is so small. I also hate how all these characters have changed. Granted people do change, so fictional ones should too, but after, say...200 or 2000 years, I think you pretty much are who you are and I wasn't seeing that with my favorites, they were a shadow of what I remembered and loved about them. <br /><br />In the end this book and I think this author isn't for me any more.</span>

  <span id="freeText1559944533354292101" style="display:none">I'm proud to say that I made it to a healthy half way point of 175 pages before giving up. <br /><br />The final nail in this coffin (heh) comes from the realization that:<br /><br />1. Nothing is happening. <br />2. All the vampires act the same, including speech patterns and overall demeanor, regardless if they are 3,000 or 50 years old. You know what would make an old vampire more believable to me? Really, really obscure knowledge. Quoting Shakespeare doesn't give me confidence that said dude has been around for thousands of years.<br />3. There is only one vampire scientist who claims all the others cannot grasp scientific knowledge. Bullshit. <br />4. Lestat, a vampire hundreds of years old, cannot remember to charge an iPhone and forgets his email login (!) and phone numbers of his friends (!!!). You are suppose to be hyper intelligent, right? You can fly on the clouds and and absorb vast amounts of knowledge but you cannot remember.... Aw, fuck it. <br /><br />And thus ends my journey with Anne Rice. Just don't forget to read all her other books. Don't worry, she'll remind you of their titles and relevance in this book so you can be sure to give her plenty of royalties. </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1091322046" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1091322046" />
    <a title="thePromoParrot" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3541711-thepromoparrot"><img alt="thePromoParrot" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583242681p2/3541711.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1091322046?book_show_action=true">Oct 28, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="thePromoParrot" class="user" itemprop="url" name="thePromoParrot" href="/user/show/3541711-thepromoparrot">thePromoParrot</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3541711-thepromoparrot?shelf=reviews">reviews</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1091322046" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer306745973156877215">Lestat, the blood-sucking anti-hero who made his first appearance in Interview with the Vampire almost 40 years ago and was played by Tom Cruise in the 1994 blockbuster film, returns in a frighteningly spellbinding mystery-thriller from the iconic author of over thirty novels, including the ground-breaking The Vampire Chronicles, Anne Rice.<br/><br/>Though Prince Lestat is a stand-alone book, it may well be worth re-reading Anne’s earlier books like The Vampire Lestat and The Queen of the Damned in order </span>
  <span id="freeText306745973156877215" style="display:none">Lestat, the blood-sucking anti-hero who made his first appearance in Interview with the Vampire almost 40 years ago and was played by Tom Cruise in the 1994 blockbuster film, returns in a frighteningly spellbinding mystery-thriller from the iconic author of over thirty novels, including the ground-breaking The Vampire Chronicles, Anne Rice.<br /><br />Though Prince Lestat is a stand-alone book, it may well be worth re-reading Anne’s earlier books like The Vampire Lestat and The Queen of the Damned in order to fully grasp the nature of the characters and how they all came into being. But re-acquainting oneself with the earlier books is not a must as one can still enjoy this latest offering from Anne Rice without having read them. Still, as the story begins from where The Queen of the Damned left off almost twenty-six years ago, many readers may like to go back and re-read the books.<br /><br />Prince Lestat: The Vampire Chronicles by Anne Rice is all about Lestat de Lioncourt, Armand, Akasha, Seth and the other vampires, and the changes they have to endure and what they are doing in the present. It is pertinent to note that the world they infested in 1998 is quite different from the world of today. Anne Rice painted a sweeping picture of how they are coming to terms with everything that happened to them, especially with Lestat, who is no longer what he once was. With huge responsibility on his shoulders as the leader of the tribe, he is constantly confronted with debilitating situations, as the vampires are at war with themselves.<br /><br />All in all, Prince Lestat: The Vampire Chronicles is spine-tingling, surprising and compelling read. It is what you can expect only from Anne Rice. The stunning world of vampires, their nature and character once again come into full play as Anne Rice shows the stuffs the wondrous world of vampire is made of.</span>
  <a data-text-id="306745973156877215" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1100742893" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1100742893" />
    <a title="Joshua" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14093977-joshua"><img alt="Joshua" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605477993p2/14093977.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1100742893?book_show_action=true">Nov 08, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joshua" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joshua" href="/user/show/14093977-joshua">Joshua</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1100742893" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16066457208630814375">What a lovely book. It's perhaps not as deep and thoughtful as Interview or Memnoch, but it's solid. Anne Rice has still got it. <br/><br/>It's been a while since I last read Queen of the Damned, but I never felt lost at any point in this book. It's like no time had passed and every character was just as familiar as they had been years and years ago when I had first gotten into this series.<br/><br/>I like the multiple voices. This book has the same structure as Queen of the Damned, which is nice because not only d</span>
  <span id="freeText16066457208630814375" style="display:none">What a lovely book. It's perhaps not as deep and thoughtful as Interview or Memnoch, but it's solid. Anne Rice has still got it. <br /><br />It's been a while since I last read Queen of the Damned, but I never felt lost at any point in this book. It's like no time had passed and every character was just as familiar as they had been years and years ago when I had first gotten into this series.<br /><br />I like the multiple voices. This book has the same structure as Queen of the Damned, which is nice because not only do we get to see how all these vampires have been getting along in the new millennium, but it's a way to refresh everyone's memory.<br /><br />The plot is very simple. A mysterious Voice has been speaking to vampires the world over, inciting confusion and violence among vampires young and old, and Lestat, the famous Brat Prince, is thrust into a position where he must uncover what the Voice is.<br /><br />This novel doesn't have the grand scope of more historical Vampire Chronicles entries like The Vampire Armand or Blood and Gold, but it definitely deals with big huge concepts, especially regarding the nature of vampires. Since the world is now one of scientific discovery, Rice has her vampires begin to move away from superstition and thoughts of religious damnation and begin to figure out what science can reveal about what makes them what they are. It's fascinating to see the blend of the supernatural and the scientific and how it's handled by the characters.<br /><br />In terms of action, this book is more concerned with characters struggling with ideas. There are moments of dramatic conflict, of course, but the main conflict is between Lestat and the Voice, which is mostly internal, so don't expect a knock down drag out explosive superhero-style climax. <br /><br />Mostly, it's just nice to see all these characters again, and see how they've adapted to a world that is now 40 years removed from that moment in the late 70's when Daniel sat down with Louis in San Francisco with a tape recorder to interview a vampire. I especially enjoyed Lestat's complaints about email and smartphones.<br /><br />Also, if you're coming to this book after a long hiatus, Anne Rice includes an appendix of names and overviews of the 10 other Vampire Chronicles books in the back to refresh your memory. The prologue, also, brings readers up to speed very well, so don't feel like you'll be completely lost if you just jump right into this one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16066457208630814375" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1087316107" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1087316107" />
    <a title="Chern Ning Xin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17076871-chern-ning-xin"><img alt="Chern Ning Xin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589098368p2/17076871.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1087316107?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chern Ning Xin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chern Ning Xin" href="/user/show/17076871-chern-ning-xin">Chern Ning Xin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17076871-chern-ning-xin?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1087316107" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer274056588257354304">I thought I would give the book 5 stars. This book was, after all, a treat. I think all of us had accepted that <i>Blood Canticle</i> was the end of <i>The Vampire Chronicles</i> - the author herself certainly thought so at one point in time. But then the publication of <i>Prince Lestat</i> was announced and we all waited in anticipation for the book that would revive Lestat, and with him, the old cast of characters. <br/><br/>But the book was disappointing. After all the hype about the characters coming together again, the a</span>
  <span id="freeText274056588257354304" style="display:none">I thought I would give the book 5 stars. This book was, after all, a treat. I think all of us had accepted that <i>Blood Canticle</i> was the end of <i>The Vampire Chronicles</i> - the author herself certainly thought so at one point in time. But then the publication of <i>Prince Lestat</i> was announced and we all waited in anticipation for the book that would revive Lestat, and with him, the old cast of characters. <br /><br />But the book was disappointing. After all the hype about the characters coming together again, the actual execution was lacklustre and mechanical. They were there, but they felt like a collection of faceless individuals to form the backdrop of the book and provide the necessary numbers in support of Lestat. When they were in the same room, they rarely interacted with each other, as though the history between them was inconsequential. I'm not sure if Armand even spoke a word to Marius.<br /><br />But even their role as supporting characters was threatened with the (to no one's surprise) introduction of several new characters, adding to the already fantastically large class of characters. It was painful to read so many pages devoted to explaining them in depth, while the established characters were continually sidelined and accounted for with a brief, cursory remark. It was particularly aggravating: it was the old cast that had me anticipating the book, after all. Instead, reading the book, now I know all about Rose and Fareed and Viktor, but what do I know of Armand? Simply where he lives, and how he fends off the young vampires who attempt to invade his home. And believe me, that's about the extent of his role in <i>Prince Lestat</i>. And what of Benji? That he has an internet radio show; this was actually a pretty interesting idea that was unfortunately restricted to Benji repeating the same thing over and over. And Sybelle is playing her piano. Sybelle is always playing her piano. <br /><br />That said, we do have minor (very minor; minor as in previously unnamed) characters from the old books fleshed out, like Antoine. But he was also unfortunately reduced to becoming part of the backdrop once he has served his purpose. He now joins Sybelle in playing music. :) <br /><br />And Lestat... where do I begin? He calls himself Lestat, alright. But reading <i>The Vampire Lestat</i> and <i>Prince Lestat</i> side by side, it is apparent that the revived Lestat is a pale shadow of his former self. I'm not even sure how to explain this. But I walked away without feeling as amused as I had been previously, no longer charmed by his antics. This new Lestat feels foreign, like a clever imitation, but ingenuine nonetheless. Are you really Lestat? <br /><br />There are many other things I could say about the book: its brave but superficial attempt at reconciling the supernatural with science (which also resulted in the (literal) production of a new character in a WTF moment) and the number of times a reference to the wonderful and holy iPhone was made. (Do all vampires use iPhone? I certainly didn't see a Nokia or a Samsung.) <br /><br />Do I regret reading this book? Probably not. At the very least, it erases the tragic and disastrous ending that was <i>Blood Canticle</i>. But do I feel let down after eagerly awaiting it all through promos? I have to admit, yes.</span>
  <a data-text-id="274056588257354304" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1094927043" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1094927043" />
    <a title="Branwen Sedai *of the Brown Ajah*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5701086-branwen-sedai-of-the-brown-ajah"><img alt="Branwen Sedai *of the Brown Ajah*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600525490p2/5701086.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1094927043?book_show_action=true">Nov 01, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Branwen Sedai *of the Brown Ajah*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Branwen Sedai *of the Brown Ajah*" href="/user/show/5701086-branwen-sedai-of-the-brown-ajah">Branwen Sedai *of the Brown Ajah*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5701086-branwen-sedai-of-the-brown-ajah?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1094927043" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5429004820740615438"><i>"For this you were born. And you are with us and one of us, and we are the people of the moon and the stars. We are not damned. We never were. Who under the sun had the right to damn any living breathing creature?"</i><br/><br/>After the death of Akasha, the vampire Queen, vampires old and young fled and became scattered across the planet. Leaderless, divided, they are like lost children. Lestat, the brat prince and rebel vampire has been avoiding others of his kind. Until he begins to hear a disembodied voic</span>
  <span id="freeText5429004820740615438" style="display:none"><i>"For this you were born. And you are with us and one of us, and we are the people of the moon and the stars. We are not damned. We never were. Who under the sun had the right to damn any living breathing creature?"</i><br /><br />After the death of Akasha, the vampire Queen, vampires old and young fled and became scattered across the planet. Leaderless, divided, they are like lost children. Lestat, the brat prince and rebel vampire has been avoiding others of his kind. Until he begins to hear a disembodied voice inside his head. When he meets with other vampires he learns to his dismay and surprise that others are hearing this 'Voice' as well. And the Voice is urging the vampires to rise up and destroy each other. Who is this Voice and what does it want? <br /><br />I once despaired of ever reading a new book featuring Lestat, Louis, Armand, Marius, Pandora, and all the other characters I have grown to love during the Vampire Chronicles series. Anne Rice hasn't written in this world in so very long. First she went through that terrifying Bible-thumper phase, and then after that she wrote the Wolf Gift books. Which I absolutely adore, don't get me wrong. But I had assumed that never again would I read something new and fresh from this series. So I was over the moon excited when I heard she was writing this book. But at the same time, I worried. Would it hold up to my expectations? Would I find the characters drastically changed since the last time I read about them? Would they even still BE the same characters, in any way shape or form? But as I slowly and languorously made my way through this book I let out a sigh of gratitude and joy. The Queen was back. It was like she had never been gone. Anne Rice's writing is just as fluid, descriptive, and beautiful as I remember. Maybe even more so. Take this passage for example:<br /><br /><i>The café was beautiful with tables draped in blue linen that was almost the color of the night sky with the endless illumination of the great sprawling metropolis bouncing off the layer of moist cloud. And there was a thin, sweet sitar music playing with melodic threads lacing in and out of my thoughts as we sat there, each of us not playing with our food and now and then lifting a forkful of curry to savor the aroma. And the wine was bright and glistening in the sheer glass goblets...</i><br /><br />See? Even just a simple passage like that holds such exquisite and beautiful description! This book was pure heaven to read! Aside from the writing itself the book was amazing because it was told from the point of view of various characters, ones I have loved for a long time and brand new ones. <br /><br />But perhaps the BEST part of this book, at least for me, was the ending. I won't spoil anything, but if you are a fan of the Vampire Chronicles you already know what an introspective and melancholy character Louis is. Well, his point of view is the one that ends it, and to see this character FINALLTY get closure, after ALL this time. It made me cry. It really did. Louis finally found his joy and his peace. <br /><br />I absolutely loved this book to pieces and I recommend it to anyone who is a fan of Anne Rice, particularly her Vampire Chronicles series.<br /><br /><i>"This is a magnificent world. And we are blessed with the gift of life in it. Let the moon and the stars always remind you of this-that though we are tiny creatures in this universe, we are filled with life."</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="5429004820740615438" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1097111984" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1097111984" />
    <a title="Jon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35426860-jon"><img alt="Jon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411962253p2/35426860.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1097111984?book_show_action=true">Nov 04, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jon" href="/user/show/35426860-jon">Jon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1097111984" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15185321246267959374">This was dreadfully boring to read. Anne Rice loves to over describe the most mundane things. I did not notice it as much in her earlier novels, but in later novels, it is more apparent. This book is not an exception. I don't mind description, but Jesus Christ, can she allow a little wiggle room for my own imagination, please?<br/><br/>Prince Lestat features characters that I do not care about and some are given their own narratives. I am not a fan of jumping back and forth between narratives. Also, most </span>
  <span id="freeText15185321246267959374" style="display:none">This was dreadfully boring to read. Anne Rice loves to over describe the most mundane things. I did not notice it as much in her earlier novels, but in later novels, it is more apparent. This book is not an exception. I don't mind description, but Jesus Christ, can she allow a little wiggle room for my own imagination, please?<br /><br />Prince Lestat features characters that I do not care about and some are given their own narratives. I am not a fan of jumping back and forth between narratives. Also, most of the dialog and character voices sound/read painfully similar. Lestat is not even a very likable character and certainly not my favorite of the series. In my opinion, the series should have ended after book 3. <br /><br />The final nail in the coffin for me was just the sheer fact that the flow was very off in this book. While descriptive, typical of Anne Rice, it did not "feel" like her work. I don't know if this was rushed to please long standing fans who have been begging her to return to this series, or if a ghost writer was used? Something was just off, that's the best way I can describe it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15185321246267959374" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1096690868" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1096690868" />
    <a title="Andromeda M31" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5455923-andromeda-m31"><img alt="Andromeda M31" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1576630346p2/5455923.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1096690868?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andromeda M31" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andromeda M31" href="/user/show/5455923-andromeda-m31">Andromeda M31</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1096690868&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1096690868" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3069745180401724486">Well, where to start. Anne Rice abandoned her Vampire Chronicles about a decade ago after her conversion to the Catholic Faith. She ended her saga with Blood Canticle, a bizarre wrap up of plot threads from her two heathen series, the Vampire Chronicles and the Lives of the Mayfair Witches. Many of her popular vampire characters were set aside or unmentioned while Lestat, her Brat Prince, declared his desire for Sainthood. Blood Canticle ended with Rowen Mayfair begging Lestat to perform the Dar</span>
  <span id="freeText3069745180401724486" style="display:none">Well, where to start. Anne Rice abandoned her Vampire Chronicles about a decade ago after her conversion to the Catholic Faith. She ended her saga with Blood Canticle, a bizarre wrap up of plot threads from her two heathen series, the Vampire Chronicles and the Lives of the Mayfair Witches. Many of her popular vampire characters were set aside or unmentioned while Lestat, her Brat Prince, declared his desire for Sainthood. Blood Canticle ended with Rowen Mayfair begging Lestat to perform the Dark Trick and allow her entry into the world of eternal darkness. As proof to his improved nature, Lestat refused and abandoned his beloved to life and mortality. Mic drop. <br /><br />Fans of the series were incredibly disappointed with that novel. Rice responded to her detractors with the line they were "interrogating the text from the wrong perspective." <br /><br />In Prince Lestat, we return to our beloved and insufferable blond hero who is once again isolated and suicidal, but as always immaculately dressed. We are introduced to a mysterious Voice that keeps him company in one of his dark rages. This telepathic Voice has been whispering to all Vampire-kind, urging the them to destroy other Blood Drinkers. <br /><br />It takes about two pages for anyone who has read the Chronicles to realize this Voice is Amel, the spirit force that fused with Akasha in the Queen of the Damned to create the Blood Drinking Race. He hasn't been mentioned, let me check, in the nine books that followed. <br /><br />And Amel isn't the only character to be brought forth from the pages of earlier books, almost every vampire Anne Rice ever wrote into undead life makes an appearance. All your favorites will get cameos, such as Armand, Pandora, Louis, Marius, David Talbot, and Jesse, but also characters that were only footnotes in the earlier Chronicles will reappear. The vampire hag that gave Lestat the metaphor the "Devil's Road" is back and alive. Turns out Marius' nameless Celtic Maker also survived to found the Talamasca. Oh, and Magnus, Lestat's dead maker, will shake hands with his fledgling as a ghost. Other ancient vampires are introduced, none of whom are interesting or different from the current caste. Their stories and chapters take up far too much space in the book. Thank God that Lestat's dear mother, Gabrielle, makes an appearance as the one vampire with a distinct personality. She slaps some sense into her son. Literally. Rice takes a brave step and adds a vampire doctor/mad scientist to her undead populace. He performs all sorts of morally ambiguous tasks in the name of science, such as making a living clone of Lestat. But there you go. Anne Rice and science. <br /><br />It's unfortunate Rice opens this book with quotes from her previous work. It showcases how far her prose has fallen. The Chronicles are mentioned several times within Prince Lestat, as they are in universe publications, and it gives her the chance to awkwardly praise her own work from a character's perspective. <br /><br />The characters that get the shortest shrift in this story are surprisingly the matriarchs Maharet and Mekare. I have always had a soft spot for the red-headed witch twins, the only female characters of definite power in Rice's endless crowd of Bryonic male heroes. Alas, the great Maharet is easily slaughtered by the weak willed villain of this story while Mekare is revealed as a mindless machine. <br /><br />It turns out the events of the Queen of the Damned are directly responsible for the current Blood Drinker Genocide. Having been placed into the barely sentient Mekare, Amel is awakened and miserable, confined in Mekare's tomb of a human body. The beautiful symmetry of Mekare taking the mantle and brain of the Queen in the earlier tales is destroyed. <br /><br />This is climaxes, of course, when Lestat sucks Mekare's brain from her eye socket and merges with the red Lovecraftian monster that is Amel and becomes Prince of Vampires. As Amel lovingly tells Lestat: he'll never be alone again. Rice writes this as a joyous union but it's a disturbing end for a character who so valued his independence and freedom. Lestat now bears the yoke of leader and sets down laws for Vampire-kind. He will rule from his restored chateau in France. Never again will Blood Drinkers separate and isolate themselves from each other; they will stand united under their Prince. <br /><br />Where Blood Canticle ended with Lestat sparing his love interest an immortal lifetime of blood sucking, Prince Lestat ends with the ceremonious vampire birth of his clone son Victor and his adopted daughter Rose. Vampires are no longer to be damned creatures of the night, but merely another tribe of beings in Rice's Savage Garden. Even Louis, the vampire most distraught at his undead existence, re-awakens to life and meaning, and no longer sees himself as damned. <br /><br />I don't particularly know where Rice will go from here with her Vampires. Prince Lestat truly feels like a grand send off, unlike Blood Canticle. Well, as grand as one can expect from a vampire series that began in the 70's written by an author who could never keep her characters straight. I've always been frustrated with the moral loop hole of the "I only kill bad people so it's okay" vampire. One of Rice's themes throughout her work is redemption, but it's apparently only allowed for beautiful and wealthy immortals who appreciate aesthetics, not for the ugly, poor, and badly dressed evildoers those vampires always seem to feed on. <br /><br />This book is only recommended for long time fans of the series. They know what to expect and will be thrilled at the reappearance of each vampire All-Star. No one else will be interested in this story. There was a time when Rice was a brilliant author. Interview with a Vampire is a fantastic and disturbing historical tale. The Vampire Lestat is a wonderful pop culture book that brought the Vampire to the Rock and Roll stage. Queen of the Damned is weird supernatural tale that brings to mind H.R. Haggard, with all his racist connotations. But for the Vampire Chronicles, trust me, stop reading there. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3069745180401724486" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16828707752473487895">I said several times that I'm a big fan of Anne Rice and all her Vampire Chronicles but to be totally honest, with after her return to the vampires I felt a bit disappointed. I think this novel is very entertaining but for my taste, the genre has too much of "thriller" and too little of "terror" and I've hardly seen any trace of the decadent romanticism of Anne Rice earlier works.<br/><br/>Spanish version:<br/>En varias ocasiones he dicho que Soy gran fan de Anne Rice y en especial de sus cónicas vampíricas, p</span>
  <span id="freeText16828707752473487895" style="display:none">I said several times that I'm a big fan of Anne Rice and all her Vampire Chronicles but to be totally honest, with after her return to the vampires I felt a bit disappointed. I think this novel is very entertaining but for my taste, the genre has too much of "thriller" and too little of "terror" and I've hardly seen any trace of the decadent romanticism of Anne Rice earlier works.<br /><br />Spanish version:<br />En varias ocasiones he dicho que Soy gran fan de Anne Rice y en especial de sus cónicas vampíricas, pero para ser sincero, éste libro me ha decepcionado. Echaba mucho de menos sus libros de vampiros y esta última entrega me ha sabido a poco. Creo que la novela es entretenida pero para mi gusto el género tiene demasiado de "thriller" y poco de "terror" y apenas he visto algún rastro del romanticismo decadente de sus anteriores obras.</span>

<div id="review_1120935504" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1120935504" />
    <a title="Mizuki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16842102-mizuki"><img alt="Mizuki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1368277474p2/16842102.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1120935504?book_show_action=true">Dec 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mizuki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mizuki" href="/user/show/16842102-mizuki">Mizuki</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=it-is-okay">it-is-okay</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=i-guess-not">i-guess-not</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=it-is-a-bad-descison">it-is-a-bad-descison</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=it-is-not-the-book-it-is-me">it-is-not-the-book-it-is-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=lost-interest">lost-interest</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=read-only-when-running-out-of-book">read-only-when-running-out-of-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=vampires-related">vampires-related</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=nothing-special">nothing-special</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=supernatural-stuff">supernatural-stuff</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1120935504" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10923954990885977351">I love Anne Rice's <i>The Vampire Chronicles</i> and <i>Lives of the Mayfair Witches</i>, the first three books of The Vampire Chronicles, together with books such as <i>The Vampire Armand</i> and <i>Blood and Gold</i>, and the first two books of the Mayfair Witches have always been my all time favorite, but this one...this <i>Prince Lestat</i> is just a big no-no.<br/><br/>But at first, I was okay with this book, we get a brief reminder of the history of the vampires, we get the mysteries of The Voice and the young vampires around the wor</span>
  <span id="freeText10923954990885977351" style="display:none">I love Anne Rice's <i>The Vampire Chronicles</i> and <i>Lives of the Mayfair Witches</i>, the first three books of The Vampire Chronicles, together with books such as <i>The Vampire Armand</i> and <i>Blood and Gold</i>, and the first two books of the Mayfair Witches have always been my all time favorite, but this one...this <i>Prince Lestat</i> is just a big no-no.<br /><br />But at first, I was okay with this book, we get a brief reminder of the history of the vampires, we get the mysteries of The Voice and the young vampires around the world being burnt to death, we get different characters telling their different stories. I like the mentions of young vampires such as Benjamin Mahmoud and how the blood drinkers deal with the modern age of Internet and technology. It's actually nice to see Leastat in all his Brat Prince's glory, it's actually nice to get into Rice's world of supernatural once again, I like her worldview and the voice of the characters, I even like the few twists in the book <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[such as how Lestat somehow fathered a son and so on <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. <br /><br />However, by page 250 I started to get annoyed and become dissatisfied with how the story and the characters are going, such as:<br /><br />(1) It bugs me that most of the narrations are done by the male characters, only one young woman named Rose manages to get her own narration, although Rose's story is interesting to an extend, it is not very engaging and it offers us no insight whatsoever.<br /><br />(2) The longer I read the book, the more all of those male vampires and their stories bled together into a blur. <br /><br />(3) There's no sparkle nor eroticism to be found within the interaction and love between different male vampires. Guy vampire loves another guy vampire? It was groundbreaking and highly erotic when Interview With the Vampire first came out, but by now it's old news. <br /><br />(4) Of course, Rice can still not write about female loving another female, to save her life.<br /> <br />(5) I absolutely hate what Rice had done to <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Maharet and Mekare. I mean, Maharet doesn't deserve to die so miserably after being separated from her twin and suffered for so long. It's disappointing for Mekare to be viewed by her twin and everyone else as nothing but a mindless monster! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />(6) Jesse Reeves and David Talbot become nothing more than bystanders by the middle of the book, and Talamasca has only be mentioned in passing.<br /><br />(7) It's annoying that women cannot be an active and successful ruler even when she possesses the power, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[because only men can be active and ruling and be comfortable with his position as ruler/leader. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />(8) In the end, I don't like how the vampires are supposed to be 'a tribe' and everyone just "Yes, we're vampires, we kill people for a living, and we're fine and productive people, actually". Suddenly vampires are all positive now instead of being creatures who are struggling to deal with their nature and their dark past and failure and flaws.<br /><br />Hell, no.<br /><br />(9) Lestat becomes a massive Gary Stu. *sighs* It's too painfully obvious that Rice loves Lestat too much, ways too much.<br /><br />(10) The Voice and its thoughts are as annoying as a spoiled teenager.<br /><br />(11) I hate the ending, I hate how <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Lestat becomes the Prince of vampires and how the mortals Viktor and Rose just become vampires and live Happy Ever After after this. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />(12) Last but not least, I also don't like how Rice insists on showing Marius as a good guy without any flaws. It's tiresome.<br /><br />If the ending part of the book isn't so disappointing, i would have given this book 3 or 4 stars.<br /><br />PS: This book is the winner of Goodreads Readers' Choice 2014? Good grief!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10923954990885977351" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7598039621490679394">2 1/2 Stars <br/>This read has had over a week to marinate and while Rice's writing style has remained eloquent and descriptive, her brand still visible, the story itself was just not enough.<br/><br/>Lestat has calmed to the point where he now reminisces and is finding he is quite lonely.<br/><br/>I was dismayed when other characters from previous books made their unwelcome appearance and, to my ultimate displeasure, decided to stick around a bit and tell their stories.<br/><br/>This story talks a lot about Akasha, the queen, he</span>
  <span id="freeText7598039621490679394" style="display:none">2 1/2 Stars <br />This read has had over a week to marinate and while Rice's writing style has remained eloquent and descriptive, her brand still visible, the story itself was just not enough.<br /><br />Lestat has calmed to the point where he now reminisces and is finding he is quite lonely.<br /><br />I was dismayed when other characters from previous books made their unwelcome appearance and, to my ultimate displeasure, decided to stick around a bit and tell their stories.<br /><br />This story talks a lot about Akasha, the queen, her blood, new vampires feeling abandoned, being a vampire in general, and this "Voice" of a vampire not understanding this new world.<br /><br />I saw where the story was going and I was not excited by it. The meat of the story did not take place until the end and was not enough to spark, the much needed life, into this wonderful remembered world.<br /><br />This story roamed and grazed, but never bucked or ran, making this read bearable, to say the least.<br /><br />Unless you are a hardcore Rice fan, I'd keep it moving.</span>

<div id="review_1096619801" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1096619801" />
    <a title="Nathan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8110005-nathan"><img alt="Nathan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1434928087p2/8110005.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1096619801?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nathan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nathan" href="/user/show/8110005-nathan">Nathan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1096619801" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8327860830031607064">Let's start by saying that I was torn between rating 2-3 stars.<br/><br/>I love The Vampire Chronicles as a whole, yes there are a few books in the series that aren't as strong as the others but as a whole Anne Rice has created a world and feel that redefined vampire fiction.<br/><br/>Unfortunately this book doesn't feel part like it's part of that world (much like Blood Canticle and Blackwood Farm). The vampires in this book, Lestat included, feel neutered and a bit flat. <br/><br/>The introduction of many new and secondary</span>
  <span id="freeText8327860830031607064" style="display:none">Let's start by saying that I was torn between rating 2-3 stars.<br /><br />I love The Vampire Chronicles as a whole, yes there are a few books in the series that aren't as strong as the others but as a whole Anne Rice has created a world and feel that redefined vampire fiction.<br /><br />Unfortunately this book doesn't feel part like it's part of that world (much like Blood Canticle and Blackwood Farm). The vampires in this book, Lestat included, feel neutered and a bit flat. <br /><br />The introduction of many new and secondary if not tertiary characters seemed unnecessary and confusing at times. <br /><br />The plot itself is basically Queen of the Damned part 2 but without any of the edge of your seat what's going to happen or interesting history of the twins. <br /><br />Now for my thoughts on some specifics....SPOILERS BELOW:<br /><br /><br /><br />A son...really?! It just seems so out of the blue and unrealistic. I appreciate the introduction of the vampire scientists because it makes sense that they would want to learn about themselves but the rushed creation of this Viktor seemed out of place. Somehow a 300 yr old vampire sperm can impregnate a human? Was I reading Twilight?<br /><br />Maharet, Mekare AND Khayman die!? ...again really? 3 of the most powerful ancient vampires get killed within sentences and that's that? How many vampires did we read about who were burned but didn't die and someone like Maharet dies this easily?<br /><br />My biggest gripe with this book is the villain (the Voice...aka Amel) turns out be an alright guy who just basically wants to feel and learn about the world. So basically this character was the vampire version of Marvel's Dark Phoenix. Previous info about Amel is wrong, he forces other vampires to kill each other and then by the end of the book he and Lestat are now best buds on the together for the long haul.<br /><br />I really just hate stories where everyone gets what they want and all ends well. This felt so neatly wrapped up that the overall plot sort of fizzled out.<br /><br />Lestat has lost some of that razzle dazzle over the years, he's become less interesting and now that he's basically the vampire god king of "the tribe" he's been put in an even less interesting place.<br /><br />This was a fun, fast read but if you're looking for the old gothic world that Anne previously created this isn't it.<br /><br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="8327860830031607064" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1525640410" />
    <a title="Thomas Edmund" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2976142-thomas-edmund"><img alt="Thomas Edmund" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1540097981p2/2976142.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1525640410?book_show_action=true">Jan 25, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas Edmund" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas Edmund" href="/user/show/2976142-thomas-edmund">Thomas Edmund</a>
      </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1525640410" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3919376550869456693">Man I used to love the Vampire Chronicles. Bought almost everything single book, and truth be told desperately wanted to be a child of the night myself (and this was well before Twilight came out, please). Although I felt the series petered off towards the end I remember them fondly and honestly thought they were to be no more.<br/><br/>So yeah, imagine my reaction when I saw this book on a shelf. Another one? I couldn't wait to get my hands on it!<br/><br/>At first it seems pretty darn good. Lestat's voice was cle</span>
  <span id="freeText3919376550869456693" style="display:none">Man I used to love the Vampire Chronicles. Bought almost everything single book, and truth be told desperately wanted to be a child of the night myself (and this was well before Twilight came out, please). Although I felt the series petered off towards the end I remember them fondly and honestly thought they were to be no more.<br /><br />So yeah, imagine my reaction when I saw this book on a shelf. Another one? I couldn't wait to get my hands on it!<br /><br />At first it seems pretty darn good. Lestat's voice was clear as ever, and I was curious about the mysterious voice. things started to go a little haywire within a couple of chapters. Everything seemed too general, the vampire world was described as being in crisis about 1,000 times but there didn't seem to be a definitive scene to explain what was happening exactly. Lestat visits a scientist vamp, which was an interesting twist, but once again, what they are up to is described in vague terms by Lestat who doesn't care for the jargon (while I agree that this fits with the character it also felt a bit hard to get intrigued by the sequence because nothing was particularly clear)<br /><br />I see that others have enjoyed the middle of the novel, however I did not. many many characters are introduced and their backstories filled out, in a fashion which simply made me questions what the novel was about, rather than connect with them. Once the story gets back on track for the last 100 pages it began to get compelling again, but the ending again was lukewarm. All the things from the original chronicles that I liked were missing, Pandora and Marius' relationship, Louis struggling with the death of Claudia, Armand's battle with his beliefs. If the book had focused on the original characters for the amount of time as the new ones I would have been much happier.<br /><br />I see that there are more books coming and I won't be giving up, but I had to be honest about this review. Here's hoping Blood Paradise raises the stakes (sorry)</span>
  <a data-text-id="3919376550869456693" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('nFX3qoHpO0KiqEH2Dq5DERTdUODSnMl8lPFe6wN56/A4zlvwLAiB50Dd3DvP37E1R9EeHD4+oAq+V5EmtVaYzQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('8Vbl//FDFVCGM3kWjMaP6Lpc9e0F5HHu4BwMws13VkdVzUmlXKKv9WRG5NtNt33M6VC7EelGGJjKusMPe1gleg==')})
  }
//]]>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/7577.Anne_Rice">About Anne Rice</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">

<a href="/author/show/7577.Anne_Rice">Anne Rice

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer7384749896455745291">Anne Rice (born Howard Allen Frances O'Brien) is a best-selling American author of gothic, supernatural, historical, erotica, and later religious themed books. Best known for <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/search?utf8=%E2%9C%93&query=The+Vampire+Chronicles' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Vampire Chronicles</a>, her prevailing thematical focus is on love, death, immortality, existentialism, and the human condition. She was married to poet <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/222961.Stan_Rice' title='Stan Rice' rel='nofollow noopener'>Stan Rice</a> for 41 years until his death in 2002. Her books have sold near</span>
  <span id="freeText7384749896455745291" style="display:none">Anne Rice (born Howard Allen Frances O'Brien) is a best-selling American author of gothic, supernatural, historical, erotica, and later religious themed books. Best known for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/search?utf8=%E2%9C%93&amp;query=The+Vampire+Chronicles" rel="nofollow noopener">The Vampire Chronicles</a>, her prevailing thematical focus is on love, death, immortality, existentialism, and the human condition. She was married to poet <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/222961.Stan_Rice" title="Stan Rice" rel="nofollow noopener">Stan Rice</a> for 41 years until his death in 2002. Her books have sold nearly 100 million copies, making her one of the most widely read authors in modern history.<br /><br />She uses the pseudonym <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/17553.Anne_Rampling" rel="nofollow noopener">Anne Rampling</a> for adult-themed fiction (i.e., erotica) and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/437669.A_N_Roquelaure" rel="nofollow noopener">A.N. Roquelaure</a> for fiction featuring sexually explicit sado-masochism.</span>

Yet, he makes Claudia a vampire, trapping her womanly passion, will, and intelligence inside the body of a small child. Louis remembers Claudia\'s struggle to understand herself and the hatred they both have for Lestat that sends them halfway across the world to seek others of their kind. Louis and Claudia are desperate to find somewhere they belong, to find others who understand, and someone who knows what and why they are.\n\nLouis and Claudia travel Europe, eventually coming to Paris and the ragingly successful Theatre des Vampires--a theatre of vampires pretending to be mortals pretending to be vampires. Here they meet the magnetic and ethereal Armand, who brings them into a whole society of vampires. But Louis and Claudia find that finding others like themselves provides no easy answers and in fact presents dangers they scarcely imagined.\n\nOriginally begun as a short story, the book took off as Anne wrote it, spinning the tragic and triumphant life experiences of a soul. As well as the struggles of its characters, Interview captures the political and social changes of two continents. The novel also introduces Lestat, Anne\'s most enduring character, a heady mixture of attraction and revulsion. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43758.The_Queen_of_the_Damned"><img alt="The Queen of the Damned (The Vampire Chronicles, #3)" style="height: 75px;" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1327871992l/43758._SY75_.jpg" />

<script>
//<![CDATA[
      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_43758'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43758.The_Queen_of_the_Damned?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">The Queen of the Damned (The Vampire Chronicles, #3)<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/7577.Anne_Rice?origin=series_works\">Anne Rice<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p6\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p0\"><\/span><\/span> 3.88 avg rating &mdash; 138,081 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 1988\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer15803344413961906876\">Librarian\'s note: An alternate cover edition can be found here\n\nIn 1976, a uniquely seductive world of vampires was unveiled in the now-classic Interview with the Vampire . . . in 1985, a wild and voluptous voice spoke to us, telling the story of The<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText15803344413961906876\" style=\"display:none\">Librarian\'s note: An alternate cover edition can be found here\n\nIn 1976, a uniquely seductive world of vampires was unveiled in the now-classic Interview with the Vampire . . . in 1985, a wild and voluptous voice spoke to us, telling the story of The Vampire Lestat.  In The Queen of the Damned, Anne Rice continues her extraordinary &quot;Vampire Chronicles&quot; in a feat of mesmeric storytelling, a chillingly hypnotic entertainment in which the oldest and most powerful forces of the night are unleashed on an unsuspecting world.Three brilliantly colored narrative threads intertwine as the story unfolds:- The rock star known as Vampire Lestat, worshipped by millions of spellbound fans, prepares for a concert in San Francisco.  Among the audience--pilgrims in a blind swoon of adoration--are hundreds of vampires, creatures who see Lestat as a &quot;greedy fiend risking the secret prosperity of all his kind just to be loved and seen by mortals,&quot; fiends themselves who hate Lestat\'s power and who are determined to destroy him . . . - The sleep of certain men and women--vampires and mortals scattered around the world--is haunted by a vivid, mysterious dream: of twins with fiery red hair and piercing green eyes who suffer an unspeakable tragedy.  It is a dream that slowly, tauntingly reveals its meaning to the dreamers as they make their way toward each other--some to be destroyed on the journey, some to face an even more terrifying fate at journey\'s end . . . - Akasha--Queen of the Damned, mother of all vampires, rises after a 6,000 year sleep and puts into motion a heinous plan to &quot;save&quot; mankind from itself and make &quot;all myths of the world real&quot; by elevating herself and her chosen son/lover to the level of the gods: &quot;I am the fulfillment and I shall from this moment be the cause&quot; . . . These narrative threads wind sinuously across a vast, richly detailed tapestry of the violent, sensual world of vampirism, taking us back 6,000 years to its beginnings.  As the stories of the &quot;first brood&quot; of blood drinkers are revealed, we are swept across the ages, from Egypt to South America to the Himalayas to all the shrouded corners of the globe where vampires have left their mark. Vampires are created--mortals succumbing to the sensation of &quot;being enptied, of being devoured, of being nothing.&quot; Vampires are destroyed.  Dark rituals are performed--the rituals of ancient creatures prowling the modern world.  And, finally, we are brought to a moment in the twentieth century when, in an astonishing climax, the fate of the living dead--and perhaps of the living, all the
